  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_64cfe83c-0eb4-4d9a-94f0-68255e4e6f82'
      });

This time she may get more than she bargained for.<br /><br />Marsilia, the local Vampire Queen, has learned that Mercy crossed her by slaying a member of her clan—and she's out for blood. But since Mercy is protected from direct reprisal by the werewolf pack (and her close relationship with its sexy Alpha), it won't be Mercy's blood Marsilia is after.<br /><br />It'll be her friends'.</span>

<a href="/user/show/16307856-kittykat-jo-tortitude">kittykat (Jo Tortitude)</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi. I agree. This whole series is urban fantasy with a very slow burn romance as a sub-subplot. Personally, it's a series I read despite the romance (<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi. I agree. This whole series is urban fantasy with a very slow burn romance as a sub-subplot. Personally, it's a series I read despite the romance (which I'm not that keen on as I dislike Adam) but for everything else that happens in it. <br /><br />IMO the Alpha and Omega series which is much more romance based is a better read if that is what you are looking for. <br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div id="review_1468281740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1468281740" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1468281740?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441018369" href="/book/show/6615021-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=vampires-and-werewolves-oh-my">vampires-and-werewolves-oh-my</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1468281740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1246865442203984384">2020 Mercy Thompson series reread! Review first posted on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.FantasyLiterature.com'>www.FantasyLiterature.com:</a><br/><br/>Mercy Thompson, a part-Native American coyote shapeshifter or walker, and full-time mechanic, is still dealing with the emotional aftermath of events in <i>Iron Kissed</i>, but at least she and the local werewolf Alpha, Adam, are on the right track now. Unfortunately for them, their relationship plans promptly get interrupted: Marsilia, the mistress of the local vampire clan or “seethe” (I love that word), has found out</span>
  <span id="freeText1246865442203984384" style="display:none">2020 Mercy Thompson series reread! Review first posted on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.FantasyLiterature.com">www.FantasyLiterature.com:</a><br /><br />Mercy Thompson, a part-Native American coyote shapeshifter or walker, and full-time mechanic, is still dealing with the emotional aftermath of events in <i>Iron Kissed</i>, but at least she and the local werewolf Alpha, Adam, are on the right track now. Unfortunately for them, their relationship plans promptly get interrupted: Marsilia, the mistress of the local vampire clan or “seethe” (I love that word), has found out that Mercy acted contrary to her orders in <i>Blood Bound</i> and is out now for Mercy’s blood, quite literally. Marsilia has a set of crossed bones painted on Mercy’s garage door (in magical, non-removable paint) that tells the supernatural world Mercy is a marked woman and free game. All in all, it’s a good time for Mercy to leave town for a few days while her werewolf friends try to negotiate a peaceful resolution with the vampires. <br /><br /> So when Mercy’s old college friend, Amber, turns up on her doorstep asking for her to come visit and help with a ghost that’s haunting her Spokane home, it seems like a heaven-sent opportunity. With all of Mercy’s current issues with vampires, it seems Mercy and Adam to be helpful that there’s only one vampire in the entire city of Spokane, one Jim Blackwood. Surely Mercy won’t come to Blackwood’s notice? But in reality, it’s out of the frying pan and into the fire.<br /><br /> This fourth book in the MERCY THOMPSON series is my favorite one yet, with tight, intense plotting and an imaginative story line that deftly mixes together ghosts, vampire conspiracies and power games, and fae artifacts all playing role in the plot, along with Mercy’s developing relationship with the long-suffering Adam. Despite all of these competing elements, the plot never gets confusing. Patricia Briggs manages to blend these elements together in a way that not only makes sense but is deeply satisfying.<br /><br />It’s a particular strength in this series that Mercy ― as well as other characters ― don’t get to simply dance through life without paying the fiddler. Emotional and psychological problems aren’t simply resolved within a week, wrapped up with a neat bow and put away forever. In fact, one major issue that I had with <i>Iron Kissed</i>, that the ending too easily smoothed over a weighty personal issue of Mercy’s, was resolved by the beginning of <i>Bone Crossed</i>, which casts that scene in a different light as the story continues from that same point.<br /><br /> One of the reasons the MERCY THOMPSON series is so appealing to me is the way that Briggs pulls in plot threads from prior books in the series. Time and again, unforeseen consequences and fallout from incidents in previous books in the series resurface, as it becomes apparent that not only are there some loose ends from the past, but they’re creating quite a tangle for Mercy and her friends. Mercy is dealing with the second and third order effects of her past actions, which is fantastic writing as far as I’m concerned. <br /><br />Similarly, characters and iconic items that the reader is already familiar with, like a particular fae walking stick, reemerge to affect Mercy’s life in new ways. For example, her ability to see ghosts, which was previously a key element in <i>Blood Bound</i>, becomes relevant once again as she attempts to help her old friend Amber with a worrisome haunt, and then further develops into an integral part of Mercy’s ongoing story. Either Briggs has plotted out this series extremely carefully, or she’s particularly gifted at reexamining prior books’ plots and finding intriguing ways to carry incidents, characters and themes forward. In either case, it all feels very organic and natural, helping to create an unusual feeling of realism in this urban fantasy world.<br /><br />After thinking about this some more, I'm upping my rating from 4 stars to 5. This book, and the series, deserves it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1246865442203984384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_110528671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110528671" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110528671?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780441016761" href="/book/show/3413662-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=shifter">shifter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library-hardcover">my-library-hardcover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110528671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer923728995300415991">Another satisfying installment in the Mercy series, although there was somewhat of the flavor of an in-between book about it. That's not really a criticism from me; when you are in a series for the long haul, it makes sense to take a breather and deal with all the events your characters have faced as well as integrate a feel of the everyday into their lives. At the end of <i>Iron Kissed,</i> there were at least two significant events that needed follow-up and I would have been disappointed in Briggs as</span>
  <span id="freeText923728995300415991" style="display:none">Another satisfying installment in the Mercy series, although there was somewhat of the flavor of an in-between book about it. That's not really a criticism from me; when you are in a series for the long haul, it makes sense to take a breather and deal with all the events your characters have faced as well as integrate a feel of the everyday into their lives. At the end of <i>Iron Kissed,</i> there were at least two significant events that needed follow-up and I would have been disappointed in Briggs as a writer and as a woman if she didn't allow her character recovery time.<br /><br />Mercy's attempting to manage her panic attacks when she gets a surprise visit from her mom that unfortunately coincides with a drop-in visit from Stefen, hungry and emaciated. The wolves help Stefen, but it's the first sign that Marsilia, the vampire queen, knows about what happened to Andre in <i>Blood Bound.</i> Mercy's business and the wolves will become targets as well. Strangely, at the same time, a frenemy from college shows up at Mercy's door looking for help dealing with a ghost harassing her son. For the good of all, Mercy decides to travel to Amber's home, with Stefen shadowing her as support in case she runs into the infamous vampire Blackwood.<br /><br />The first time I read this, pacing felt very irregular to me. But that's kind of a bonus, as series tend towards predictable arcs. Still, there's some strange authorial choices--Stefan, Mercy's mom and Amber all showing up at the same time? Peculiar, and the sort of stuff that says "hello, red herring" to the reader in an overly dramatic way. The relationship progresses in generally positive ways. Adam gives Mercy more than enough space, except late in the book when he panics. I thought it a nice balancing act of characterization, as it avoids the 'perfect boyfriend/imperfect girlfriend' baloney and shows that Adam makes mistakes as well.<br /><br />Once again, except for surface conversations with frenemy Amber, Mercy has no real female bonding moments. Everyone--and thing--is male. If it's female, it is not a friend. Seriously, Briggs? What's with the authorial choice there? Reading these stories back to back makes it painfully obvious that there's some odd mental schism in the author's world. I think it ended up contributing to me dropping the series, because in between life-threatening events, it's mostly about Mercy's emotions surrounding her male relationships. All that said, Marsilia continues as one of the most fascinating and complex characters, even if she's prefer to see Mercy dead.<br /><br />Three and a half stars, rounding down because... women.</span>
  <a data-text-id="923728995300415991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38217487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38217487" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38217487?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780441016761" href="/book/show/3413662-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">UF lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=werewolf">werewolf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-adore">heroine-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=supercouple">supercouple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=good-secondary-characters">good-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=ghost">ghost</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=shapeshifter">shapeshifter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2015-action-adventure-challenge">2015-action-adventure-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=native-american-folklore">native-american-folklore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38217487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1505462097033407146">Patricia Briggs continues to impress me with her oh-so expressive writing that conveys so much, so economically. I am truly in awe of her talent. Clearly I am very behind on this series. It's not due to a lack of appeal, but due to my reading style and my review reading taking up a lot of my reading time. But I do love knowing that I have a guaranteed read when I reach for one of her books.<br/><br/>Mercy is definitely near the top of my list of fictional characters I think I would love to have as a frien</span>
  <span id="freeText1505462097033407146" style="display:none">Patricia Briggs continues to impress me with her oh-so expressive writing that conveys so much, so economically. I am truly in awe of her talent. Clearly I am very behind on this series. It's not due to a lack of appeal, but due to my reading style and my review reading taking up a lot of my reading time. But I do love knowing that I have a guaranteed read when I reach for one of her books.<br /><br />Mercy is definitely near the top of my list of fictional characters I think I would love to have as a friend in real life. Probably number one, if I'm honest. And not just because she's an excellent and trustworthy mechanic (and I need one of those big time). Mercy is a mix of real-life traits: humble, down-to-earth, courageous (even in the face of fear, which is the true definition of courage), snarky, empathetic, observant, and very self-deprecating. While some readers don't like abuse storylines in their books, I don't mind them when they are done well. Mercy shows so much strength and fortitude of character. Her journey to recovery after her attack in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1412138.Iron_Kissed__Mercy_Thompson___3_" title="Iron Kissed (Mercy Thompson, #3) by Patricia Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Iron Kissed</a> is realistic and inspiring. I truly love this woman.<br /><br />Briggs writes the kind of fantasy that grabs hold of me and doesn't let go. She plants a garden of what seems like ordinary wildflowers, but exotic blooms that are far from ordinary grow in that garden, waiting to be plucked by a reader. Briggs mixes shapeshifters, werewolves, fae, and vampires in an appealing way that doesn't leave out the inherent menace of all the various supernatural creatures. With a coyote shifter narrator, the reader is fully along for the ride, as Mercy is the first to admit that being a coyote shifter doesn't always give her the advantage, but often puts her in a dangerous situation (while she is more immune to magic than most, she's not impervious.) Oh, and Briggs also throws in ghosts. I must say that I was happy as a clam, since I love fantasy like a house on fire, but I also have an appreciation for old school/classic horror and an old-fashioned ghost story.<br /><br />Can I take the time to gush over the men in Mercy's life? <br /><br /> Adam, Adam, Adam! How I love you. He is perfect for Mercy. And I like that Mercy is starting to see past her emotional wounds and barriers to see him for who he is, her Mate. Also, I love that Adam is so patient and loving about it, even though that is an act of hard-won discipline. He's very possessive, but not in a controlling, irritating way. I love a possessive hero like a house on fire, but I find controlling, dominating men a turnoff. Adam is just right for me. I wish I had an Adam in real life! He's very demonstrative that Mercy is his, but he's not trying to dictate to her every step she takes. He's a true life partner.<br /><br />If there was no Adam in the Mercy Thompson world, then I would definitely be all over Samuel. I still love Samuel, very much. I just don't love him for Mercy's mate. I love him all on his own, and I hope he gets the Mate he needs one day. He's a really cool character. Sweet as pie, but also full of danger that makes the hair stand up on one's neck. He seems serious, but has this mischievous sense of humor. His calm facade hides a wild wolf that might never be tamed.<br /><br />Bran is the Man, or rather, the Alpha of the Alphas (Marrok). He steals a scene, no matter who else is in it. And that's saying something in this series! I know Briggs has said she probably won't write a book with Bran as a main character. I'm sad and understanding of that. He's such a mysterious and compelling figure, when he shows up, it's so satisfying but also tantalizing. I can't love him more. I'm always hungry for more of him.<br /><br />Stefan has actually grown on me quite a bit. While I have become quite a vampire romance fan, I still prefer shifters/weres to vampires, and I like that they take center place in this series. But Stefan adds such a nice touch to this series. While he insists on telling Mercy that he is a 'very bad man', his actions say otherwise. I haven't decided who would play my Stefan, but it would have to be an actor with lots of presence. I liked how Briggs develops Mercy's friendship with Stefan much more in this book (it was more assumed at the beginning). I have to say the vampire storyline makes my heart beat fast and gives me shivers. They are truly menacing creatures.<br /><br />The thing with Briggs is that no character is a throwaway. Each one is carefully developed, even for their short presence in this book. You feel everything even in a short scene that you should feel. And while the characters might throw you for a loop at first, their motivations are apparent as the layers peel away.<br /><br />I think that for the short length of this book, it's really a full meal. Urban fantasy for the true lover of the genre. Also, I think a good gateway to those who are investigating this genre for the first time. Mercy by herself is enough to keep a reader hooked. But the secondary characters, the plotting and storyline will have the reader staying for seconds and dessert.<br /><br />Highly recommended! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1505462097033407146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/752102385" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/752102385?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752102385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10662717347049922045">Re-read Time. I'm slowly buy surely making my way through the series again.<br/><br/><b>Second Read Review</b><br/><br/>So apparently, I don't remember anything from this series. I completely forgot who the bad guy was, or anything about the vampire politics at play or the main plot of the story. The only thing I remembered at all was some superficial stuff about Adam and Mercy's relationship. <br/><br/>It's a little strange that I don't remember more of this series, it is almost like I never read them before. <br/><br/>Still the bad guy was</span>
  <span id="freeText10662717347049922045" style="display:none">Re-read Time. I'm slowly buy surely making my way through the series again.<br /><br /><b>Second Read Review</b><br /><br />So apparently, I don't remember anything from this series. I completely forgot who the bad guy was, or anything about the vampire politics at play or the main plot of the story. The only thing I remembered at all was some superficial stuff about Adam and Mercy's relationship. <br /><br />It's a little strange that I don't remember more of this series, it is almost like I never read them before. <br /><br />Still the bad guy was bad, ghosts are a little scary, vampires suck, Stephan is okay though, Mercy needs to protect everyone, Adam has a temper (that we never ever see), the Pack doesn't like Mercy being a part of them and <b>Mercy's milkshake brings all the boys to the yard</b> even though she tells us all the time how un-special she is. <br /><br />Yep I think that a bout covers it. I think I'll drop half a star to 3.5 stars. There is a lot of repetition that doesn't really need to be in there and Mercy's need to protect Adam and the wolves is silly sometimes, they are werewolves I'm pretty sure they can protect themselves.<br /><br /><b>Original Review</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“One of the oddest things about being grown-up was looking back at something you thought you knew and finding out the truth of it was completely different from what you had always believed.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Well isn’t that true. Mercy has always felt like she was on the outside looking in and alone. Raised by the wolves she was still never part of the pack, little did she know how important she was to Bran the Alpha of all Alphas. When she accepted Adam as her mate she never really knew what that would mean. Now that she is part of the pack it isn’t really what she expected it to be. It is hard to have people in your head when you have felt alone most of your life.<br /><br />Marsila has figured out that Mercy had something to do with the death of her demon raising vampire and is out to get her. But since Mercy is now protected by the pack Marsila has to find a new way to punish her. In an effort to help her pack and an old college friend, she heads out of town to help with a ghost problem. Stefan tags along to look after her while Adam sorts out the problems with Marsila. But it seems that the only vampire in town there might have other plans for her.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Only you could go to Spokane and get bitten by the one vampire in the whole city.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Mercy, Mercy, Mercy you find trouble in the darnedest places, it seems Adam can’t let you out of his sight for a minute. It was only supposed to be a ghost problem but it seems that the ghost that is haunting a little boy is more than Mercy planned for.<br /><br />I always like that the Mercy Thompson books are always more than they seem. There are a few layers to everything that is going on. This one in particular was interesting because there was the Vampire in Spokane that wants something from Mercy as well as Marsila and her political maneuverings that involve Stefan. Marsila is crafty and vengeful to say the least. The storyline was well thought out and there were quite a few instances that I was worried for characters. <br /><br />Other than that I like all the side things that are going on that may or may not come into play later. There is the walking stick that seems to like Mercy and follows her around, her cat that likes vampires, werewolves and coyotes, a book on fae and Mercy’s ability to find trouble around every corner.<br /><br />I was happy to see more of Stefan he is one of my favorite characters, he is the Spike (everyone should know who that is) of the series.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“That’s a pretty lame superhero name,” I told him.<br />“Scooby-Doo is already taken,” he said with dignity. “Anything else sounds lame in comparison.”</i>
</b> <br />He is the Vampire who doesn’t really have a heart of gold but…..he is better than most. I love his weird obsession with Scooby-Doo<br />This is still a super fun series. I enjoyed getting so see a little relationship progression with Mercy and Adam because I &lt;3&lt;3&lt;3 them together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10662717347049922045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12464772598985484351"><b>Re-read for the 3rd time April 12th 2020.</b> Already onto the next one!<br/><br/><b>Re-read March 24th, 2017. </b><br/><br/>Mercy manages to attract a lot of trouble and chaos, I guess that might be part of her nature as a Coyote. <br/><br/>After the events of the last book Mercy suffers panic attacks and some hesitatancy even though she knows Adam would never hurt her, but all that takes a back seat when Marsilia finds out about Andre.   <span id="freeText12464772598985484351" style="display:none"><b>Re-read for the 3rd time April 12th 2020.</b> Already onto the next one!<br /><br /><b>Re-read March 24th, 2017. </b><br /><br />Mercy manages to attract a lot of trouble and chaos, I guess that might be part of her nature as a Coyote. <br /><br />After the events of the last book Mercy suffers panic attacks and some hesitatancy even though she knows Adam would never hurt her, but all that takes a back seat when Marsilia finds out about Andre. And most are completely ruthless. However, Mercy and her wolves shouldn't be underestimated.<br /><br />There's an uneasiness with the Pack because of Mercy, something that factors into future stories. Love how Adam always has her back!</span>

<div id="review_1830024361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830024361" />
    <a title="samantha  (books-are-my-life20)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27251572-samantha-books-are-my-life20"><img alt="samantha  (books-are-my-life20)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468163897p2/27251572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_42521991" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42521991" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42521991?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie (jjmachshev)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie (jjmachshev)" href="/user/show/882708-julie-jjmachshev">Julie (jjmachshev)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780441016761" href="/book/show/3413662-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/882708-julie-jjmachshev?shelf=2009-reads">2009-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42521991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8150524683532729">Mercy, mercy, Mercy! Patricia Briggs latest Mercy Thompson novel "Bone Crossed" kept me on the edge of my seat, furiously reading to find out what happened next! There's good news and bad news in Mercy's latest adventure and just when you think things will settle down, BAM, there's someone new looking to mess with Mercy's peace.<br/><br/>Mercy is still recovering from her brutal rape at the hands of a fae 'possessed' wacko. Mercy managed to kill the b^%tard, but it will be a while before the psychological</span>
  <span id="freeText8150524683532729" style="display:none">Mercy, mercy, Mercy! Patricia Briggs latest Mercy Thompson novel "Bone Crossed" kept me on the edge of my seat, furiously reading to find out what happened next! There's good news and bad news in Mercy's latest adventure and just when you think things will settle down, BAM, there's someone new looking to mess with Mercy's peace.<br /><br />Mercy is still recovering from her brutal rape at the hands of a fae 'possessed' wacko. Mercy managed to kill the b^%tard, but it will be a while before the psychological scars heal, if ever. The good news is that she's finally decided to mate with Adam. The bad news is she's not sure how long it will take before she can get close to him without a panic attack. The good news is he's willing to wait and help her recover. The bad news is her friend Stefan the vampire appears suddenly and close to real death, just having time to say "She knows". That means the vampire Queen is aware that Mercy managed to kill not one, but two of her creatures...and now she wants Mercy's blood, and not just for a snack.<br /><br />I think my heart rate is still elevated after this one. I have to rate this series as one of my absolute fave fantasies, right up there with Hamilton and Ward. The difference with Briggs is that I let my sons read these stories (PG fating)! A strong heroine, shapeshifters, fae (they're NOT the fae from your childhood stories either), vampires, creatures of lore, and a pagan god or two make their way into Briggs' stories and Mercy's world...and it all flows together smooth as silk. Now I have to wait another year for my next fix!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8150524683532729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1947484006" />
    <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books"><img alt="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415550632p2/5892196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1947484006?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books">Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22816618-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=purchased">purchased</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1947484006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12900833908634036392">This review can also be found at <a href='http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life in Books</a>.<br/><br/>I enjoyed this book even more during this re-read. This is definitely one of my all time favorite series and I honestly believe that everyone who hasn't read these books yet should run to the bookstore right away and buy them up. This is the fourth book in the Mercy Thompson series and it picks up right after the events of the previous book. It is really important that this series be read in order since some of the events are carried</span>
  <span id="freeText12900833908634036392" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life in Books</a>.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book even more during this re-read. This is definitely one of my all time favorite series and I honestly believe that everyone who hasn't read these books yet should run to the bookstore right away and buy them up. This is the fourth book in the Mercy Thompson series and it picks up right after the events of the previous book. It is really important that this series be read in order since some of the events are carried over from the previous book. I really had a lot of fun with this audiobook.<br /><br />On major focus of this Adam and Mercy's relationship. They both really do care for each other and want to make things work. I like how carefully they are with each other. Mercy is a mess after the horrible events of the previous book and Adam is there for her. He really wants to help with her pain and if he could I am sure he would take it away. <br /><br />The mystery in the story is centered around vampires. I like the vampires in this world so that works out well for me. The local vampires have painted crossed bones on the door at her garage and she decides it would be a good idea to get out of town for a bit. Her friend from college has a little problem with a ghost so Mercy goes to help...and runs into more than she bargained for. Stefan plays a large role in this book and really proved how much he cares for Mercy as well.<br /><br />I love Lorelei King's narration of this series. I am amazed by how well she voices all of these characters and keeps things consistent from book to book. The emotional aspects of the story really come through during her narration. I was able to listen to this book for hours at a time largely due to her wonderful delivery of this story. Lorelei King is quickly becoming one of my favorite narrators. <br /><br />I would highly recommend this series to other. This was my second time experiencing this book and I hope to read it again in the future. It is really that good. <br /><br /><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br />Lots of vampires in this one. Mercy was awesome as always!<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561631923?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6512051-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=review-books-done">review-books-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=poc">poc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561631923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2844031366327019785">February 2018 Reread: Buddy read with Sarah and Erica :)<br/>January 2017 Re-read: Buddy read with Sarah<br/><br/>January 2016 Re-read: Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498356433' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah</a>: I've never really loved this book as much as the previous 2 in the series, before. But this re-read was different for me. It was stronger here. I appreciated the villain, and the story, and everything that was happening. Mercy needed this time, needed this moment - especially after the events of the last book. And - even though this is one of the worst v</span>
  <span id="freeText2844031366327019785" style="display:none">February 2018 Reread: Buddy read with Sarah and Erica :)<br />January 2017 Re-read: Buddy read with Sarah<br /><br />January 2016 Re-read: Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498356433" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a>: I've never really loved this book as much as the previous 2 in the series, before. But this re-read was different for me. It was stronger here. I appreciated the villain, and the story, and everything that was happening. Mercy needed this time, needed this moment - especially after the events of the last book. And - even though this is one of the worst villains she's faced yet - it was, to me, a welcome reprieve after the heart-wrenching moments in the last book. Not that there aren't plenty of them here. After all, one doesn't heal immediately from the events at the end of <i>Iron Kissed</i>.<br /><br />Even though Mercy spends some time away from the Tri-Cities, we get plenty of development with her relationships - with everyone. And I love that.<br /><br />Original Review:<br />Mercy's barely a week out from the tragic events that happened at the end of Iron Kissed when Stefan pops in at her feet, a blackened husk, whispering "She knows."<br /><br />With vampires stalking her steps and pressing vague attacks on the werewolves in her life, Mercy decides to take a trip to help a friend with a ghost. Of course, it just couldn't be that simple and Mercy finds herself in a much scarier predicament.<br /><br />Not quite as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/285205.Blood_Bound__Mercy_Thompson___2_" title="Blood Bound (Mercy Thompson, #2) by Patricia Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Bound</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1412138.Iron_Kissed__Mercy_Thompson___3_" title="Iron Kissed (Mercy Thompson, #3) by Patricia Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Iron Kissed</a>, but still a pretty solid read. The "mystery" story-line wasn't as appealing to me, but there's so much development with the characters (Mercy and Adam in particular, with quite a bit from Stefan) that I can't help but enjoy this every time.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6512491119848294967">I think I had a fairly good run. I managed to read two whole books before becoming once again severely put out with/by Mercy Thompson.   <span id="freeText6512491119848294967" style="display:none">I think I had a fairly good run. I managed to read two whole books before becoming once again severely put out with/by Mercy Thompson. This at least, lets me know that it was not my finicky mood that caused me to dislike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71811.Moon_Called__Mercedes_Thompson___1_" title="Moon Called (Mercedes Thompson, #1) by Patricia Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Moon Called</a> rather, there are honest to goodness irritants imbedded in Mercy’s character description and narration that annoys this shit out of me. <br /><br />First let me state how appalled I am by the fact that Briggs allowed her rapped heroine to have sex only a week after her rape. WTF? Second, Briggs wrote far too many inconsistencies for me to believe that Mercy was either traumatized or healing from her rape. One minute she is having panic attacks, the next she is wagging her bare ass at her dull lover as he looks on from across the room. Again I ask, WTF? And further shame to Briggs for dragging out a sex scene between Adam and Mercy for four books, only to have it fade to black. At least own it if you are going to include it. Christ. I’m going to stop now because I’m working myself into a heated frenzy just thinking about it. You annoyed me Ms. Briggs, and this was your second chance. I doubt there will be a third.<br /><br />*Side Note*<br />Stefan, I still love you, even though you suffer in poor taste, given that you are in lurve with Mercy and all, but I forgive you as I suspect you are merely a casualty of piss poor character development.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1145051300" />

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=kick-ass-ladies">kick-ass-ladies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=i-see-dead-people">i-see-dead-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1145051300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11175318476109139510"><b> *** 4 ***</b><br/><br/>This installment in the Mercy world seemed to be more of a refining and a bridging book. After the horrible and devastating experiences Mercy had in the last book, the author decided that she, as well as us, the readers, need a bit of recovery and regrouping time. She does that by slowing the pace a bit and letting Mercy and the wolfs work on developing their relationship. She also found a way to intensify Stephan's connection with the little coyote (poor vampire had to go through real</span>
  <span id="freeText11175318476109139510" style="display:none"><b> *** 4 ***</b><br /><br />This installment in the Mercy world seemed to be more of a refining and a bridging book. After the horrible and devastating experiences Mercy had in the last book, the author decided that she, as well as us, the readers, need a bit of recovery and regrouping time. She does that by slowing the pace a bit and letting Mercy and the wolfs work on developing their relationship. She also found a way to intensify Stephan's connection with the little coyote (poor vampire had to go through real torture courtesy of the vamp mistress), and the magic walking stick kept cuddling up with her every chance it got and followed her about like a pup. <br /><br />The focus of the story this time was on Mercy getting over the emotional trauma, which had left her with paralyzing panic attacks at random moments and her almost aversion to touch... It is also sad how helpless she feels every time another one of her always powerful enemies takes away her will, thus re-traumatising her over and over!!! Who would not start doubting their strength and sanity under such circumstances??? But her weaknesses are what makes us root for her and her ability to dust herself off and despite her fears, get herself up and fighting again, are what makes her our hero... <br /><br />Reading this was not as easy and engaging as the previous book, but it was layered with characters, feelings and situations with which I am sure the author is laying the foundation for the stories to come. I am aflutter with anticipation and having all the published volumes of the series, I am jumping into the next at once! Have a fun time reading to all!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11175318476109139510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1573378332" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1573378332" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1573378332?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780441016761" href="/book/show/3413662-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=werewolves-shifters">werewolves-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=public-library">public-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1573378332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13431413241151205473"><b>2018 Re-read:</b><br/><br/>One of my favourite Mercy Thompson novels! Lots of vampire drama, but most importantly we get to know Stefan better. Is it wrong that I still wish Mercy had chosen him rather than Adam? Mercy gets to really draw on her skinwalker powers, proving once again that being a growly werewolf is not necessarily as tough as the wily coyote! (BTW, I saw a big fluffy coyote over the Xmas holidays, and thought of Ms. Thompson).<br/><br/>Re-reading this series has really re-set my internal reading-metre. </span>
  <span id="freeText13431413241151205473" style="display:none"><b>2018 Re-read:</b><br /><br />One of my favourite Mercy Thompson novels! Lots of vampire drama, but most importantly we get to know Stefan better. Is it wrong that I still wish Mercy had chosen him rather than Adam? Mercy gets to really draw on her skinwalker powers, proving once again that being a growly werewolf is not necessarily as tough as the wily coyote! (BTW, I saw a big fluffy coyote over the Xmas holidays, and thought of Ms. Thompson).<br /><br />Re-reading this series has really re-set my internal reading-metre. I’m enjoying myself again, recovering from a potential reading slump before it really got hold of me. Thank you, Ms. Briggs, for giving me that oomph to escape the downward pull of the book-slump-undertow!<br /><br />****<br /><b>Original review</b><br /><br />Finally, Stefan is back on the scene, still mysterious in motive, but protective to our heroine, Mercy. And that is despite his treatment by the local vampire seethe. (Isn’t that a great collective noun for vampires?) <br /><br />This is also the book that sees Mercy make her choice between werewolves Adam and Samuel. I’m somewhat disappointed that she had to choose, rather than remaining independent. So often, once a choice is made, the sexual tension drains out of a series and it becomes less interesting. I will be interested to see how Briggs maintains the forward momentum.<br /><br />Also of interest, Mercy continues to discover the special powers of a skinwalker that make her anathema to the mainstream vamps. She is extremely fortunate to have Stefan as a friend &amp; protector and I hope this means that he will continue to appear in future volumes.<br /><br />I still maintain that Mercy needs some women friends, and not like her friend Amber who shows up in this installment. She needs some strong, good women in her life to help her sort out all the demanding men in her world.<br /><br />Once again, the cover art makes me shake my head. Who in the world are they trying to appeal to? Take my word for it, Mercy looks nothing like the covers.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3279660345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10684366959855892765">Briggs excels at characters. It drew me to her traditional fantasy and serves her even better in the longer series format. You come back to a series to see what the characters are doing now, because their lives absorb you and you want to know how things turn out for them. Her characters a multi-dimensional, engaging people and I can’t think of one who I’d wish she’d kill off.<br/><br/>One thing that makes me sad about this series is it shifts focus between creatures. I love that Blood Bound and Bone Cross</span>
  <span id="freeText10684366959855892765" style="display:none">Briggs excels at characters. It drew me to her traditional fantasy and serves her even better in the longer series format. You come back to a series to see what the characters are doing now, because their lives absorb you and you want to know how things turn out for them. Her characters a multi-dimensional, engaging people and I can’t think of one who I’d wish she’d kill off.<br /><br />One thing that makes me sad about this series is it shifts focus between creatures. I love that Blood Bound and Bone Crossed focus on the vampires since Stefan is an incredible character. He’s loyal, has a strong sense of humor, but is willing to kill innocents to further his agenda. Wulfe is still an enigma but we get the tiny glimpse more of what drives him. But focus on vampires means some other characters don’t get much screen time. Jessie barely shows up in this book, but she’s quite funny whenever she does.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/599676956" />
    <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet"><img alt="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387046887p2/13567836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/599676956?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet">Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer599676956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer286025075003134284"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Need More Adam Interference*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote> <br/><b>
  <u>Re-read: 05.07.2019</u>
</b><br/>The fourth book in the series the Volkswagen mechanic and a walker (a magical being with the power to shift into a coyote at will), <b>Mercedes ‘Mercy’ Athena Thompson</b> (how old is she?), finds herself torn between wanting Adam and what he has to offer, and not putting him in danger by being with her. On top of that, she still struggles with panic attacks from her rape in previous book <i>and</i> her killing vampire Andre has finally reac</span>
  <span id="freeText286025075003134284" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Need More Adam Interference*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote> <br /><b>
  <u>Re-read: 05.07.2019</u>
</b><br />The fourth book in the series the Volkswagen mechanic and a walker (a magical being with the power to shift into a coyote at will), <b>Mercedes ‘Mercy’ Athena Thompson</b> (how old is she?), finds herself torn between wanting Adam and what he has to offer, and not putting him in danger by being with her. On top of that, she still struggles with panic attacks from her rape in previous book <i>and</i> her killing vampire Andre has finally reached the Mistress' ears, who wants her dead. But that's not all, an old ‘friend’ of her needs her help. <br /><br />Overall, the concept is good, we get a little closer to Mercy than the previous books, but she still keeps us reads a bit a bay. <b>What I want is more romance</b>. Though I don't mean for the plot to center the romance, what I mean is that I want Mercy and Adam working together, as a <i>couple</i>, and not just Mercy on her own with Adam coming in later <i>after</i> all is said and done. I just need more. I need a relationship such as <i>
  <b>Kate Daniels</b>
</i> and <b>
  <i>Curran</i>
</b> has. To be frankly honest, I feel like the independence Mercy has kinda overshadows Adam's potential. Is that weird? That being said, this re-read made the rating go down; while it used to have 4 stars, it now has 3. But I do like to mention that I really adore Mercy and Stefan. Together. This is simply because Adam's barely <i>there</i> because Mercy keeps him at arms length.<br /><br /><b><u>Other Characters</u>:</b><br /><i>The list is long so I put it in a spoilers tag.</i><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[→ <b>Adam Hauptman</b>, the Alpha of the local werewolf pack (the Columbia Basin Pack), and his human daughter, <b>Jessica ‘Jesse’ Tamarind Hauptman</b> (15).<br />→ <b>Samuel ‘Sam’ Llewellyn Cornick</b>, his father, <b>Bran ‘The Marrok’ Cornick</b>, and his brother, <b>Charles Cornick</b>, a financial genius. In the US, all the packs follow the Marrok, a title taken from the name of one of King Arthur’s knights who was a werewolf. The Marrok and his pack have oversight of all the werewolves in North America. Bran's mate, <b>Leah</b>. Samuel is a medical doctor.<br />→ <b>Siebold ‘Zee’ Adelbertsmiter</b> of the Black Forest, Mercy's former boss, had retired when he sold her the place, but he’d come out once in a while to “keep his hand in.” He's also a Metallzauber/gremlin (fae).<br />→ <b>Medea</b>, Mercy's cat.<br />→ <b>Stefan ‘the Soldier’ Uccello</b>, a vampire and a somewhat friend of Mercy.<br />→ <b>Elizaveta Arkadyevna Vyshnevetskaya</b>, the cleanup crew leader. She was the most powerful witch in the Pacific Northwest. Her grandson, <b>Robert</b>.<br />→ <b>Tony Montenegro</b> (33 or so), a cop and Mercy's friend.<br />→ <b>Darryl Zao</b>, Adam’s second. He was a Ph.D. engineer working at the Pacific Northwest Laboratories in some sort of government hush-hush project. <b>Auriele</b>, a chemistry teacher at Richland High and Darryl’s mate.<br />→ <b>Warren</b>, one of the good guys, a hero, Mercy's favorite in Adam's pack. Warren is also Adam's best friend and most trusted in the pack, and his third. He was also a lone wolf; simply because he's gay and most of the werewolves in power in the US had been born in a time when homosexuality was anathema, even punishable by death in some places. <br />→ <b>Kyle Brooks</b>, Warren’s current lover and a divorce lawyer.<br />→ <b>Ben</b>, a werewolf in Adam's pack. British.<br />→ <b>Margi</b>, Mercy's mother, <b>Curt</b>, Mercy's stepfather.<br />→ <b>Tad</b>, Mercy's old assistant and Zee's son.<br />→ <b>Signora Marsilia</b>, Mistress of the Mid-Columbia Seethe (vampire).<br />→ <b>Mary Jo</b>, a firefighter with the Kennewick FD, and pack member to Adam.<br />→ <b>Sylvia Sandoval</b> and her son, <b>Gabriel Sandoval</b> (16). Zee fixed her car and in exchange, Gabriel will work for Mercy.<br />→ <b>Cory Littleton</b>, a vampire sorcerers who let's himself be possessed by a demon.<br />→ <b>Andre ‘the Courtier’</b>, a vampire and left hand to the Mistress (Stefan is her right hand). Mercy kills him at the end of book three.<br />→ <b>Daniel</b>, a new vampire made by Andre, though he was Stefan's when he was human. Killed by Ben but it was Littleton fault as he controlled Ben in book three.<br />→ <b>Wulfe ‘the Wizard’</b>, a vampire who looks like a teenager.<br />→ <b>Tom Black/John Beckworth</b>, a reporter/an investigative journalist. His daughter, <b>Kara</b>, survived an attack from a werewolf at the age of 10, now 3 years later her father locks her up every full moon.<br />→ <b>Honey</b>, and her mate-and-husband, a plumbing contractor, <b>Peter Jorgenson</b>, werewolves in Adam's pack.<br />→ <b>Uncle Mike</b>, owner of a bar/tavern meant for the fae. Is fae himself.<br />→ <b>Naomi</b> and <b>Rachel</b>, bloodgivers/sheeps to Stefan.<br />→ <b>Estelle ‘the Teacher’</b> and <b>Bernard</b>, old vampires belonging to the Mistress. Two of the few vampires strong enough to live on their own. The others being Stefan, Andre and Wulfe. Of the five most powerful vampires, only Stefan and Andre are truly Marsili's.<br />→ Mrs. <b>Marjorie Hanna</b>, a ghost.<br />→ Dr. <b>Stacy Altman</b>, a folklore specialist from the University of Oregon, the police's expert consultant. Is <b>the great Carrion Crow</b> (blind), one of the <b>Gray Lords</b> (the leaders of the fae)?<br />→ <b>Jean Ryan</b>, the best criminal defense attorney this side of Seattle and Zee's lawyer. She's also a member of the John Lauren Society, an anti-fae group.<br />→ <b>Tim Milanovich</b>, part of an anti-fae group. Killed by Mercy in book three after he raped her.<br />→ <b>Austin Summers</b>, leader of an anti-fae group. Tim killed him in book three.<br />→ <b>Amber Wharton</b>, had been Mercy's college roommate <b>Charla ‘Char’</b>’s best friend. <br />She and Mercy had been acquaintances rather than friends. Amber's husband, <b>Corban Wharton</b>, a moderately successful corporate lawyer about ten years her senior. <b>Chad</b> (8 or 10, this changes....), their son who's deaf - though Corban is not his biological father, a man named Harrison is.<br />→ <b>James ‘Jim’ ‘The Monster’ Blackwood</b>, the only vampire in Spokane; who kept his territory free of vampires or anything else that might challenge him. He's also Amber’s husband’s best client. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mercy, with the help of a Oak fae, kills him at the end of the book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br /><b>Genre</b>: - (Adult) Urban Fantasy (M/F)<br /><b>Series</b>: - Series, Book Four.<br /><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes, for now? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>Favorite character?</b> - Adam Hauptman.<br /><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Sure.<br /><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Sure.<br /><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - It's me... I do love re-reading. <br /><b>New Rating</b> - 3 stars (I gave it 4 stars first time reading it).</span>

<div id="review_117473882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117473882" />
    <a title="Cyna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4171731-cyna"><img alt="Cyna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356316087p2/4171731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117473882?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cyna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cyna" href="/user/show/4171731-cyna">Cyna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780441016761" href="/book/show/3413662-bone-crossed">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117473882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7095999399788664193">This is the first book where we get the dual-plotline format, presumably because Briggs liked both concepts but couldn't figure out a way to stretch them both out into book length. It's strange to have one plot advertised on the cover, and then have a completely different one make up most of the book, especially when there is nothing tying the two together, except Mercy. It must suck to have two super powerful bad guys plotting against you at the exact same time.<br/><br/>There’s nothing particularly memo</span>
  <span id="freeText7095999399788664193" style="display:none">This is the first book where we get the dual-plotline format, presumably because Briggs liked both concepts but couldn't figure out a way to stretch them both out into book length. It's strange to have one plot advertised on the cover, and then have a completely different one make up most of the book, especially when there is nothing tying the two together, except Mercy. It must suck to have two super powerful bad guys plotting against you at the exact same time.<br /><br />There’s nothing particularly memorable about Bone Crossed. Mercy is done wavering between men and has basically settled into a relationship with Adam. She is done fighting for her independence, and just accepts all the decisions that Adam makes for her where she would have at least argued one or two books ago. Because we’ve seen what happens when Mercy makes decisions for her self. It just really seems that in this book Mercy is broken. This is understandable after having been raped, but we feel that she allows to much of her self to be lost and stops fighting for the normal, uncomplicated life that she wanted to build. Instead she throws herself head first into the werewolf society she’d previously decided against by becoming a member of a pack and the Alpha’s mate.<br /><br />The manner in which Adam makes Marcy pack is probably our biggest issue with this book, and the best example of Mercy’s transformation. Having taken Stefan’s blood in Blood Bound, Mercy still has a psychic connection to him, and feels his despair upon learning that his flock has been wiped out. This triggers a panic attack in Mercy, while she is with Adam. Adam realizes why she is panicking, and without giving Mercy a choice, performs the ceremony that makes her pack, which breaks the connection to Stefan. He then states, “He can’t have you. Not now. Not ever. I don’t owe him that.”<br /><br />After calming down, Adam rightly feels that he did wrong, and should be berated for his presumption. But the new, improved Mercy is not angry. Instead, she says this:<br /><br /> “Thank you, Adam [...] Thank you for tearing Tim into small Tim bits. Thank you for forcing me to drink one last cup of fairy bug-juice so i could have use of both of my arms. Thank you for being there, for putting up with me. Thank you for keeping me from being another one of Stefan’s sheep-I’ll take pack over that any day. Thank you for making the tough calls, for giving me time. Thank you for loving me."<br /><br />WHY THANK YOU ADAM FOR MAKING ALL MY FUCKING DECISIONS FOR ME.<br /><br />This is how much Mercy has changed. Adam flat-out admits that he made her pack because he didn’t want her to have a connection with someone else (possessive much?). Even Adam realizes that this was overstepping his bounds. But Mercy thanks him. WHAT THE HELL! SHE THANKS HIM. This is another step in the breaking down of Mercy Thompson. Where previously she would have been livid and argued, she has now accepted that her man Adam knows what’s best for her.<br /><br />It’s worth noting that Mercy’s only real act of independence in this book is to decide who to subjugate herself to, Stefan or the big bad, Blackwood. Girl power...<br /><br />Read more at <a href="http://yourekilling.us/?p=151" rel="nofollow noopener">You're Killing.Us</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7095999399788664193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104354146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6444902284212038018"><b>Posted on<a href='http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2012/12/review-bone-crossed-by-patricia-briggs.html' rel='nofollow noopener'> Under the Covers</a></b><br/><br/>This is my second time reading <i>Bone Crossed</i>. Having not read the first three books the first time, I was completely lost to what was happening. I didn’t feel attached to Mercy’s character and didn’t find the romance engaging. This time around though, everything was in perspective and I found that this book was a lot “lighter” in terms of the banter between characters. Briggs really kicked up the humour in this book! I found myself stupidly smiling at the teasing between</span>
  <span id="freeText6444902284212038018" style="display:none"><b>Posted on<a href="http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2012/12/review-bone-crossed-by-patricia-briggs.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> Under the Covers</a></b><br /><br />This is my second time reading <i>Bone Crossed</i>. Having not read the first three books the first time, I was completely lost to what was happening. I didn’t feel attached to Mercy’s character and didn’t find the romance engaging. This time around though, everything was in perspective and I found that this book was a lot “lighter” in terms of the banter between characters. Briggs really kicked up the humour in this book! I found myself stupidly smiling at the teasing between Mercy and the werewolves and I noticed that Mercy’s got a smart mouth in this one! This line was particularly funny: <br /><br /><i> There was even a “Ho, ho, ho,” if you skipped around a little and deleted an “e” on the last “ho”. Our green painter had a limited vocabulary and occasionally mixed up a professional working woman with a garden implement. </i> Har har!<br /><br />One thing that’s different about this series is that the vampires don’t give off “fuck me” pheromones. Instead, they’re scary as hell, which is just as effective as keeping readers on their toes. James Blackwood creeps me out and the ending with the ghosts and zombie thing just wasn’t for me. Yuck!<br /><br />But the biggest thing about this book is probably the relationship between Mercy and Adam. While they aren’t going at it like rabbits, there’s still one scene that is particularly memorable. There’s something unique about Briggs’ writing because even though she holds off on the sex, people still read it! That to me is a testament to her writing skill. There’s so much more to Mercy and her world than just her relationships. And it’s a world I’d love to read more of.<br /><br />Favourite Quote:<br />“Just like Medea,” he murmured. “All I have to do is put my hands on you. You can be spitting mad...and then you lean against me and go all soft and still.” He put his mouth against my ear. “That’s how I know you want me as much as I want you.” His arms were tight around me, and I knew that I wasn’t the only one with wounds.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6444902284212038018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119701989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119701989" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119701989?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
